        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer257485935" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9569845345021447396">Based on a true story, THE ONE AND ONLY IVAN is the tale of a silverback gorilla who's forgotten how to be a gorilla in many ways. Raised in a house with people who fed him ice cream cones and took him to baseball games, Ivan grows rambunctious and ends up creating finger paintings as one of the star attractions in a mall circus. When Ruby, a baby elephant arrives, Ivan promises to save her from a lifetime chained in a tiny cage. To do so, he needs to reclaim his title as silverback, the leader </span>
  <span id="freeText9569845345021447396" style="display:none">Based on a true story, THE ONE AND ONLY IVAN is the tale of a silverback gorilla who's forgotten how to be a gorilla in many ways. Raised in a house with people who fed him ice cream cones and took him to baseball games, Ivan grows rambunctious and ends up creating finger paintings as one of the star attractions in a mall circus. When Ruby, a baby elephant arrives, Ivan promises to save her from a lifetime chained in a tiny cage. To do so, he needs to reclaim his title as silverback, the leader and protector of his group.<br /><br />While it's so sad in places, this is a story that will ultimately warm the hearts of animal lovers young and old. The narration (by Ivan the gorilla!) could easily have slipped into the melodramatic, but heavy doses of humor and an equal balance of heart keep it from being anything but poignant and perfect. Kids will love this book, and in the classroom, it will pair nicely with articles like this one (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.paws.org/ivan-gorilla.html">http://www.paws.org/ivan-gorilla.html</a>) about the real Ivan that inspired the story.<br /><br />I support independent bookstores. Here's a link to find one near you or to order THE ONE AND ONLY IVAN via IndieBound: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.indiebound.org/book/9780061992254/katherine-applegate/one-and-only-ivan">http://www.indiebound.org/book/978006...</a></span>

<div id="review_1325325409" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1325325409" />
    <a title="Kristen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8409451-kristen"><img alt="Kristen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513342355p2/8409451.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1325325409?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristen" href="/user/show/8409451-kristen">Kristen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8409451-kristen?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8409451-kristen?shelf=favorite-reads-of-2015">favorite-reads-of-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1325325409" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13948257449062614942">5/5 stars<br/><br/><b>The Skinny:</b><br/><br/>Ivan, a lonely silverback gorilla, has lived in the Exit 8 Big Top Mall and Video Arcade for 27 years. Ivan’s only friends are an elephant named Stella, A small dog named Bob, and a human girl named Julie. Ivan is content in his domain (as he calls it), because he does not really know any differently. One day, a new animal arrives at the struggling Big Top Mall. Ruby, a baby elephant awakens something within Ivan. Suddenly his domain doesn’t seem so warm anymore; now it seems</span>
  <span id="freeText13948257449062614942" style="display:none">5/5 stars<br /><br /><b>The Skinny:</b><br /><br />Ivan, a lonely silverback gorilla, has lived in the Exit 8 Big Top Mall and Video Arcade for 27 years. Ivan’s only friends are an elephant named Stella, A small dog named Bob, and a human girl named Julie. Ivan is content in his domain (as he calls it), because he does not really know any differently. One day, a new animal arrives at the struggling Big Top Mall. Ruby, a baby elephant awakens something within Ivan. Suddenly his domain doesn’t seem so warm anymore; now it seems like the small cage that it is.<br /><br /><b>The Review:</b><br /><br />This story was heart-warming and heart-wrenching all at the same time. My heart strings haven’t been pulled quite so much by a book this entire year.<br /><br />I don’t know how she did it, but if gorillas could truly talk, I think they would sound exactly like how Katherine Applegate wrote Ivan’s voice. Ivan, through his words and actions, came across as almost innocent throughout most of the novel. Because of his unintentional innocence, Ivan was also often humorous.<br /><br /><i>You can only throw so many me-balls at humans before you get bored. A me-ball is made by rolling up dung until it’s the size of a small apple, then letting it dry. I always keep a few on hand. For some reason, my visitors never seem to carry any. </i> Ivan is <u>completely</u> serious when he says this. <br /><br /><i>”Poor old Ivan,” she says. “I’ve been ignoring you, haven’t I?”<br />I grunt again, a dignified indifferent grunt.<br />Julia thinks for a moment, then smiles. She walks over to my domain, to the spot in the corner where the glass is broken. She slides paper through. She rolls a pencil across my cement floor.<br />“You can draw the baby elephant too,” Julia says.<br />I bite the pencil in half with my magnificent teeth. Then I eat some paper.</i><br /><br />This innocence that Ivan embodies changes after Ruby arrives. Ruby makes Ivan recognize his past, which he had shut out, and also helps him to see that the Big Top Mall is not the right place for Ruby. Ivan cares for Ruby so much that he does not want the Mall to be the last place she sees; he doesn’t want Ruby to end up like him. <br /><br /><i> “Do you think,” she asks, “that I’ll die in this domain someday…?”<br />Once again I consider lying, but when I look at Ruby, the half-formed words die in my throat. “Not if I can help it,” I say instead.<br />I feel something tighten in my chest, something dark and hot. “And it’s not a domain,’ I add. <br />I pause and then I say it.<b>“It’s a cage.”</b> </i><br /><br />If I had to pick one thing that this book is about it would be friendship. The friendships that are developed in this story are of the truest kind. They are the type that help you to grow as a person, and to challenge yourself and what you’ve always known. <br /><br />On a darker note, this book is about humanity, more specifically the nature of humans. As I read, I kept asking myself why some of us are so greedy and self-absorbed. I also wondered how people can do the things they do and still sleep at night. <br /><br /><b>Overall:</b> <br /><br />The One and Only Ivan sent for me a tail-spin; I felt both intense happiness and sadness as I read. When I picked this book off the shelf, I wasn’t anticipating the love I would have for this story. I feel like children and adults alike could find a place for Ivan and his friends in their hearts. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13948257449062614942" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('DefVT66AV+54qjGStbL+PwizA1nv2crNSWY/JtErdIxvNBdiUjugc8cz2R0ly9bFd/RsFfltmrGXD2P7I2ofDw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SDZTYQXPS4/9u3fQ+8iTK36jlkq4qkm0IeG/IorMC4cq5ZFM+XS8EkIin19rsbvRAeT5Bq4eGcj/iOP/eI1gBA==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer18440014904459586873">Katherine Applegate is the author of <i>The One and Only Ivan</i>, winner of the 2013 Newbery Medal. Her novel <i>Crenshaw</i> spent over twenty weeks on the <i>New York Times</i> children's bestseller list, and her first middle-grade stand-alone novel, the award-winning <i>Home of the Brave</i>, continues to be included on state reading lists, summer reading lists, and class reading lists.<br/><br/>Katherine has written three picture</span>
  <span id="freeText18440014904459586873" style="display:none">Katherine Applegate is the author of <i>The One and Only Ivan</i>, winner of the 2013 Newbery Medal. Her novel <i>Crenshaw</i> spent over twenty weeks on the <i>New York Times</i> children's bestseller list, and her first middle-grade stand-alone novel, the award-winning <i>Home of the Brave</i>, continues to be included on state reading lists, summer reading lists, and class reading lists.<br /><br />Katherine has written three picture books: <i>The Buffalo Storm</i>; <i>The Remarkable True Story of Ivan, the Shopping Mall Gorilla</i> (often used as a companion book to <i>The One and Only Ivan</i> for younger readers); and <i>Sometimes You Fly</i> (publishing in spring, 2018). For beginning readers, Katherine wrote <i>Roscoe Riley Rules</i>, a seven-book series.<br /><br />With her husband, Michael Grant, Katherine co-wrote <i>Animorphs</i>, a long-running series that has sold over 35 million books worldwide.<br /><br />Katherine lives in Marin County, California, with her family and assorted pets.</span>
